The Second Objection: Cannibalism and Original Parts
Al-Sanusi presents the cannibalism objection and solves it via original parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the cannibalism objection to bodily resurrection and the Ash'ari solution based on original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya).

Core Idea
Only the original parts are resurrected, not those acquired from food.

The cannibalism objection challenges bodily resurrection by asking which body gets the shared parts. This objection was historically used by skeptics and materialists. Al-Sanusi defends the doctrine by introducing the concept of 'original parts' (al-ajza' al-asliyya) that persist throughout life. In this passage, you will see the objection, the rebuttal, and a deeper discussion with scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the argument's structure emerge naturally.
The passage is dense with objections and answers; note the repetitive structure.
2
Identify the core problem
What is the cannibalism objection? How does it threaten the idea of bodily resurrection? Look for the claim that parts cannot belong to two bodies.
The objection raises issues of identity and justice.
3
Understand the solution: original parts
Al-Sanusi introduces 'al-ajza' al-asliyya' (original parts). What are they? How do they solve the problem? Notice the contrast with parts acquired through nutrition (al-taghdhiya).
Original parts are those present from birth until death.
4
Examine the scriptural response
The passage includes a quotation about reviving bones and dust. How does Al-Sanusi interpret these verses? He distinguishes between verses that remove astonishment and those that prove restoration.
This shows the importance of proper scriptural hermeneutics.
5
Compare with the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila assert that God must preserve parts for justice. Al-Sanusi says 'perhaps' (la'alla). What is the difference in theological method?
Ash'aris emphasize divine will and power; Mu'tazila emphasize divine wisdom and obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - لو أكل إنسان إنساناً فالأجزاء المأكولة إما أن تعاد في بدن الأكل، فلا يكون المأكول بعينه معاداً أو بالعكس، على أن لا أولوية، ولا سبيل إلى جعلها جزءاً من كل منهما، وأنه يلزم في أكل الكافر المؤمن تنعيم الأجزاء العاصية، وتعذيب المطيعة، ورد بأن المعاد هي الأجزاء الأصلية، فلا محذور، ولعل الله يحفظها من أن تصير جزءاً أصلياً لبدن آخر . بل عند المعتزلة يجب ذلك ليصل الجزاء إلى مستحقه . فإن قيل: مثل من يحيي العظام وهي رميم أئذا متنا وكنا تراباً يشعر بأن المتنازع إعادة الأجزاء بأسرها. قلنا لأنه ورد إزالة لاستبعادهم إحياء الرميم والتراب، والوارد لإثبات نفس الإعادة ايضاً كثير مثل : وهو الذي يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده فسيقولون من يعيدنا قل الذي فطركم أول مرة . الثاني - لو أكل إنسان إنساناً، وصار غذاء له جزءاً من بدنه، فالأجزاء المأكولة إما أن تعاد في بدن الآكل، أو في بدن المأكول، وأياً ما كان لا يكون أحدهما بعينه معاداً بتمامه على أنه لا أولوية لجعلها جزءاً من بدن أحدهما دون الآخرة ولا سبيل لجعلها جزءاً من كل منهما، وايضاً إذا كان الأكل كافراً والمأكول مؤمناً يلزم تنعيم الأجزاء العاصية ، أو تعذيب الأجزاء المطيعة. والجواب - أنا نعني بالحشر إعادة الأجزاء الأصلية الباقية من أول العمر إلى آخره، لا الحاصلة بالتغذية ، فالمعاد من كل من الأكل والمأكول الأجزاء الأصلية الحاصلة في أول الفطرة من غير لزوم فساد. فإن قيل : يجوز أن يصير تلك الأجزاء الغذائية الأصلية في المأكول الفاضل في الأكل نطفة وأجزاء أصلية لبدن آخر، ويعود المحذور. قلنا : الفساد إنما هو في وقوع ذلك ، لا في إمكانه فلعل الله تعالى يحفظها من أن تصير جزءاً لبدن آخر، فضلاً عن أن تصير جزءاً أصلياً. وقد ادعى المعتزلة أنه يجب على الحكيم حفظها عن ذلك ليتمكن من إيصال الجزاء إلى مستحقه، ونحن نقول : لعله يحفظها عن التفرق، فلا يحتاج إلى إعادة الجمع والتأليف، بل إنما يعاد إلى الحياة والصور والهيئات.
Second - If a person eats another person, the eaten parts are either restored in the body of the eater, then the eaten person is not restored as the same individual, or vice versa, without priority, and there is no way to make them a part of both bodies, and it necessitates in the case of a disbeliever eating a believer the enjoyment of the disobedient parts and the punishment of the obedient parts. It is rebutted by saying that the restored parts are the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya), so there is no problem, and perhaps God preserves them from becoming an original part of another body. Rather, according to the Mu'tazila, it is necessary for that to occur so that recompense reaches its due. If it is said: Like 'Who revives the bones when they are decayed?' 'When we are dead and become dust?' suggests that the dispute is about the restoration of all parts. We say: It was revealed to remove their astonishment at reviving decayed bones and dust, and what is revealed to prove restoration itself is also abundant, such as: 'He is the One who originates creation and then restores it' and 'They will say: Who will restore us? Say: The One who created you the first time.' Second - If a person eats another person, and the food becomes part of his body, the eaten parts are either restored in the body of the eater or in the body of the eaten, and in either case, neither one is restored exactly in its entirety, since there is no priority to make them part of one body over the other, and there is no way to make them part of both bodies, and also if the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten is a believer, it necessitates the enjoyment of the disobedient parts or the punishment of the obedient parts. The answer: We mean by resurrection (al-hashr) the restoration of the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, not those obtained through nutrition. So the restored (al-ma'ad) from each of the eater and the eaten are the original parts obtained at the first creation, without any corruption. If it is said: It is possible that those nutritional parts become the surplus in the eaten, a sperm and original parts for another body, and the problem returns. We say: Corruption is only in the occurrence of that, not in its possibility; perhaps God preserves them from becoming a part of another body, let alone becoming an original part. The Mu'tazila claimed that it is incumbent on the Wise to preserve them from that to enable the recompense to reach its due. We say: Perhaps He preserves them from dispersion, so there is no need to restore gathering and composition, but rather they are restored to life, forms, and states.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage addresses the second objection to bodily resurrection: the problem of cannibalism. If one human eats another, the consumed parts could belong to both individuals at resurrection. The objection presents several difficulties: if the parts are restored to the eater's body, the eaten person is not fully restored; if to the eaten, the eater is incomplete; there is no priority to assign them to one body; and if a believer is eaten by a disbeliever, the believer's parts would be rewarded (since they become part of the disbeliever's body) and the disbeliever's parts punished, which is unjust. The initial rebuttal states that only the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) are resurrected, not those acquired through nutrition. God may preserve those original parts from becoming original parts of another body. A further objection quotes verses that mention reviving bones and dust, suggesting that all parts are restored. The answer clarifies that these verses are meant to remove astonishment, not to prove the restoration of every particle; other verses explicitly prove restoration. The passage then repeats the objection in more detail and gives the answer: resurrection restores the original parts that persist from birth to death, not the nutritional parts. A sub-objection asks if the nutritional parts could become original parts for another body (e.g., as sperm), and the answer is that corruption lies in the actual occurrence, not the possibility, and God may preserve them. The Mu'tazila assert that God must preserve them to ensure justice, while the author says perhaps He preserves them from dispersion, so there is no need to recompose scattered parts.

Key Terms
الأجزاء الأصلية
الحشر
المعاد
التغذية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that bodily resurrection requires the exact same material particles that composed the body at death.
Correction: Al-Sanusi clarifies that only the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) are restored, not the parts acquired through nutrition or other changes.

Checkpoint
How does the author resolve the cannibalism objection?
A) By affirming that all eaten parts are restored in the eater's body.
B) By stating that only the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) are resurrected.
C) By denying that cannibalism ever occurs.
D) By claiming that the soul alone is resurrected.

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) resolves the cannibalism objection and affirms bodily resurrection while maintaining divine justice and power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What parts of your life—habits, attachments, relationships—are you counting on to be eternally 'you'? Have you considered that only your original self (your core intentionality and faith) will be restored, not your acquired accumulations? How does that change what you prioritize daily?
?
If God preserves the original parts of every person from dispersion, as Al-Sanusi argues, then your resurrection is certain. Yet do you live as if you will face every intention and action with that same core self? What have you added to your life that you assume will be resurrected as part of you, but is actually temporary?
?
The Mu'tazila demanded that God must preserve parts for justice; Al-Sanusi said 'perhaps He preserves them.' Are you demanding that God owes you a certain outcome in the afterlife, or are you trusting His will and power? Which of your expectations about the Day of Judgment is based on a sense of entitlement rather than reliance on God's mercy and wisdom?

The Objection from Cannibalism and Its Answer
Presents the second objection about cannibalism and the response distinguishing original parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that cannibalism poses for bodily resurrection and how the response distinguishes original parts from acquired parts.

Core Idea
Resurrection restores only the original parts, not those gained through nutrition.

This lesson tackles a classic objection against bodily resurrection: what happens if one person eats another? If the consumed parts become part of the eater's body, how can both be resurrected completely? The answer clarifies that resurrection concerns only the original parts that persist from birth, avoiding the dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the objection presents a logical dilemma and a moral dilemma.
2
Understand the dilemma of parts
The eaten parts cannot be returned to both the eater and the eaten simultaneously. There is no priority for one over the other, and they cannot be split. Why is this a problem for resurrection?
3
Consider the added moral problem
If the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten a believer, then the same parts would have to be rewarded (for being part of the believer) and punished (for being part of the disbeliever). This seems contradictory.
This highlights the incoherence of a naive view of bodily resurrection.
4
Study the answer
The answer defines resurrection (al-ḥashr) as restoring only the original parts that persist from birth to death, not those gained through nutrition. This resolves both dilemmas.
Observe how the definition of terms is key to resolving theological objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - لو أكل إنسان إنساناً، وصار غذاء له جزءاً من بدنه، فالأجزاء المأكولة إما أن تعاد في بدن الآكل، أو في بدن المأكول، وأياً ما كان لا يكون أحدهما بعينه معاداً بتمامه على أنه لا أولوية لجعلها جزءاً من بدن أحدهما دون الآخرة ولا سبيل لجعلها جزءاً من كل منهما، وايضاً إذا كان الأكل كافراً والمأكول مؤمناً يلزم تنعيم الأجزاء العاصية ، أو تعذيب الأجزاء المطيعة. والجواب - أنا نعني بالحشر إعادة الأجزاء الأصلية الباقية من أول العمر إلى آخره، لا الحاصلة بالتغذية ، فالمعاد من كل من الأكل والمأكول الأجزاء الأصلية الحاصلة في أول الفطرة من غير لزوم فساد.
Second: If a human eats a human, and it becomes nutrition for him a part of his body, then the eaten parts either are returned in the body of the eater or in the body of the eaten. Whichever it is, neither of the two is entirely returned as the very same, given that there is no priority for making them a part of the body of one over the other, and no way to make them a part of each of the two. Also, if the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten a believer, it would necessitate rewarding the disobedient parts or punishing the obedient parts. The answer: We mean by the gathering (al-ḥashr) the restoration of the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, not those acquired through nutrition. So the resurrected of each of the eater and the eaten is the original parts that came into being at the first creation, without any corruption necessarily following.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against bodily resurrection and its answer. The objection rests on the impossibility of reassigning consumed body parts: they cannot be restored fully to both the eater and the eaten. Furthermore, if the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten a believer, rewarding or punishing the parts becomes incoherent. The answer clarifies that resurrection ('al-ḥashr') means restoring only the original parts that persist from birth to death, not those gained through nutrition. Thus each person is resurrected from their own original parts, avoiding the dilemma.

Key Terms
الإعادة
الأجزاء الأصلية
الحشر
التغذية
المعاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think resurrection requires reassembling the exact same atoms that composed the body at death, including atoms gained from food.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only the original parts that remain from birth to death are restored; acquired parts from nutrition are not necessary for resurrection.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does 'al-ḥashr' refer to?
A) The restoration of all body parts including those acquired through nutrition.
B) The restoration of only the original parts that persist from birth to death.
C) The restoration of the soul only, not the body.
D) The resurrection of the entire body exactly as it was at death.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection restores only the original parts that accompany a person from birth to death, not those gained through nutrition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God can restore your original parts even if your body has been entirely consumed? How does this lesson challenge any doubts you might have?
?
If your identity after resurrection depends on the original parts from birth to death, what does that say about the value of your physical actions? How does this affect your view of your body as a trust from God?
?
This answer shows that no human action can thwart God's plan of resurrection. Does your heart truly accept that God's power is absolute over every detail of your life and death? What practical steps can you take to deepen that conviction?

Could Original Parts Become Another's?
Raises an objection and provides an answer about original parts becoming another's.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that original parts could become another's original parts is answered by distinguishing possibility from actuality and appealing to divine preservation.

Core Idea
Possibility does not entail actuality; God can preserve original parts intact.

This passage addresses a further objection to the doctrine of bodily resurrection with original parts. The opponent argues that even if we accept resurrection of original parts, those parts could become the original parts of another body through digestion and reproduction, bringing back the original difficulty. The answer distinguishes between mere possibility and actual occurrence, and asserts that God can preserve those parts from such transformation. The Mu'tazila argue it is obligatory for a Wise God to do so, but the author takes a more modest position: perhaps God preserves them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the objection and the answer. Notice the structure: it begins with "If it is said..." and then "We say..."
2
Identify the two parts
The passage has an objection and an answer. The objection is about original food parts becoming another's original parts. The answer first distinguishes possibility from actuality, then mentions the Mu'tazila claim and the author's position.
The answer uses 'perhaps' (لعل) which shows a cautious tone.
3
Understand the Mu'tazilite argument
The Mu'tazila claim it is obligatory for the Wise (God) to preserve the parts so that retribution can be delivered. The author agrees that preservation is possible but uses 'perhaps' rather than 'obligatory'.
Compare the different theological orientations: Mu'tazila emphasize divine justice, while the author emphasizes divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : يجوز أن يصير تلك الأجزاء الغذائية الأصلية في المأكول الفضل في الأكل نطفة وأجزاء أصلية لبدن ،آخر، ويعود المحذور. قلنا : الفساد إنما هو في وقوع ذلك ، لا في إمكانه فلعل الله تعالى يحفظها من أن تصير جزءاً لبدن ،آخر، فضلاً عن أن تصير جزءاً أصلياً. وقد ادعى المعتزلة (1) أنه يجب على الحكيم حفظها عن ذلك ليتمكن من إيصال الجزاء إلى مستحقه، ونحن نقول : لعله يحفظها عن التفرق، فلا يحتاج إلى إعادة الجمع والتأليف، بل إنما يعاد إلى الحياة والصور والهيئات.
If it is said: It is possible that those original food parts in the eaten become (by way of the eater's surplus) sperm and original parts for another body, and the problem returns. We say: The corruption is only in its actual occurrence, not in its possibility. Perhaps God Almighty protects them from becoming a part of another body, let alone from becoming an original part. The Mu'tazila claimed that it is obligatory for the Wise to protect them from that in order to be able to deliver the recompense to its deserving one. We say: Perhaps He protects them from scattering, so there is no need for re-gathering and re-composing; rather, they are only restored to life and forms and shapes.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a further objection: even if resurrection is of original parts, those original food parts could become the sperm (original parts) of another body, bringing back the same difficulty. The answer distinguishes between possibility and actuality: the corruption lies in its actual occurrence, not its mere possibility. God could preserve those parts from ever becoming part of another body, especially from becoming original parts. The Mu'tazila argued that it is obligatory for a Wise God to preserve them to ensure retribution, but the author says God might even preserve them from disintegrating, such that they do not need to be reassembled but only restored to life and form.

Key Terms
الأجزاء الأصلية
المعتزلة
الحكيم
الحفظ
التفرق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the problem is logically inescapable; the answer shows it is only a possibility that God can prevent.
Correction: The objection confuses possibility with actuality. God's power to preserve ensures the actual occurrence can be avoided, so the doctrine remains coherent.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazilite claim mentioned in the passage?
A) That God must preserve the parts because it is impossible for Him to do otherwise.
B) That it is obligatory for the Wise to preserve the parts so that retribution can be delivered.
C) That resurrection is purely spiritual and does not involve bodies.
D) That the parts will inevitably become parts of another body.

Key Takeaway
The objection to resurrection with original parts is not fatal because God can preserve them from ever becoming another's parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's power is sufficient to preserve every particle of your body for resurrection? If so, how would that certainty change the way you treat your body today? What would you stop worrying about, and what would you start taking more seriously?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted that God must act a certain way to be wise and just. Have you ever imposed your own expectations of what God 'should' do? Are you willing to trust His 'perhaps' even when you cannot see the outcome, especially regarding your own final state?
?
This lesson shows that God can prevent any obstacle to resurrection. What obstacles in your own life—sins, doubts, or attachments—do you need to trust God to remove, even if you cannot imagine how? Will you commit today to surrender that specific struggle to Him and wait on His preservation?

Responding to the Objection from Resurrection Verses
Objection from resurrection verses, response distinguishing re-creation from identity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that Quranic verses require resurrection of all body parts is answered by distinguishing between the deniers' concern and the theological subtlety of identity.

Core Idea
The verses prove God's power to re-create, not necessarily every atom.

In theological debates about bodily resurrection, opponents sometimes cite Quranic verses that mention decayed bones or dust being revived. At first glance, these seem to demand exact material continuity. However, the response shows that the intended lesson of these verses is different: they aim to remove doubt about God's power to bring back the dead, not to settle philosophical questions about the identity of particles. This passage clarifies that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verses cited
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the verses the objector uses: Q 36:78, 56:47, 34:7, which speak of decayed bones, dust, and being torn apart.
2
Understand the response's move
The response cites other verses (Q 30:27, 17:51) that emphasize God's ability to begin and repeat creation. The key is that the deniers' doubt was about the possibility of revival, not about which particles are restored.
The response does not argue against the objector's verses; it recontextualizes them.
3
Reflect on the theological nuance
Realize that the question of restoring original parts versus all parts was not the focus of the deniers. The response shows that the Quran's aim is to affirm God's power, not to settle philosophical debates about identity.
This keeps the discussion on the intended meaning of the verses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الآيات الواردة في باب الحشر من مثل : من يحيي العظام وهي رميم (۲) أئذا متنا وكنا ترابا (۳) إذا مزقتم كل ممزق إنكم لفي خلق جديد (4) . تشعر بأن الأصلية، وغير الأصلية، ومتنازع المحق والمبطل، ومتوارد الإثبات والنفي هي إعادة الأجزاء بأسرها إلى الحياة ، لا الأصلية وحدها، ولا إعادة المعدوم بعينه . قلنا: ومن الآيات ما هو مسوق لنفس الإعادة مثل : وهو الذي يبدأ الخلق ثم يعيده) (۱) فسيقولون من يعيدنا قل الذي فطركم أول مرة ) (٢) وكأن المنكرين استبعدوا إحياء ما كانوا يشاهدون من الرميم والتراب، فأزيل استبعادهم بتذكير ابتداء الفطرة والتنبيه على كمال العلم والقدرة. وأما حديث إعادة المعدوم والأجزاء الأصلية فلعله لم يخطر ببالهم .
If it is said: The verses that have come in the chapter of al-ḥashr, such as 'Who will give life to bones while they are decayed?' (Q 36:78), 'When we die and become dust?' (Q 56:47), 'When you are torn apart every tearing, you will be in a new creation' (Q 34:7) — suggest that [what is meant is] the original and non-original, that which is disputed between the right and the wrong, and that which is subject to affirmation and negation, is the restoration of all parts to life, not the original ones alone, nor the restoration of the non-existent as the very same. We say: Among the verses are those that are presented for the [act of] restoration itself, such as 'He who begins creation then repeats it' (Q 30:27), 'They will say: Who will give us life? Say: He who created you the first time' (Q 17:51). It is as if the deniers considered the revival of what they witnessed of decayed bones and dust far-fetched, so their far-fetchedness was removed by reminding them of the first creation and drawing attention to the perfection of knowledge and power. As for the talk of restoring the non-existent and the original parts, it perhaps never occurred to them.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage raises an objection from Quranic verses that seem to indicate the resurrection of all body parts, including non-original ones, and not merely the original parts. The answer points to other verses that focus on the act of re-creation itself, such as 'He who begins creation then repeats it' and 'Say: He who created you the first time.' The real issue for the deniers was the revival of decayed bones and dust, which God's power makes possible. The subtle question of restoring exactly the same or only original parts was not on their minds. Thus these verses do not force the conclusion that every atom must be restored.

Key Terms
الآيات
الحشر
الإعادة
المعدوم
الأجزاء الأصلية
الرميم
التراب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran requires exact material continuity of all parts for resurrection.
Correction: The verses focus on God's power to create anew; the question of exact particle identity was not the concern of the deniers.

Checkpoint
What is the essence of the answer to the objection from Quranic verses?
A) The verses prove that all parts must be restored exactly as they were.
B) The verses are metaphorical and do not concern bodily resurrection.
C) The deniers' concern was the revival of decayed bones, not the identity of particles, and other verses emphasize re-creation.
D) The verses only refer to original parts.

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses about resurrection primarily affirm God's power to re-create, not necessarily the restoration of every specific atom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever doubt God's power to resurrect you because you focus on your physical decay? How does this lesson challenge that doubt? What change in your heart must happen so that you trust His re-creation without needing material continuity?
?
The deniers' real concern was the impossibility of reviving decayed matter. Do you have any area of your life where you think God cannot restore because the situation seems too far gone? How does this passage call you to reflect on His ability to create anew?
?
You are shown that the verses do not settle every theological detail; they address the immediate doubt. Are you willing to trust God’s Word even when it does not answer every question you have? What does that trust look like in your daily walk?

The Objection: Resurrection Has No Proper Purpose
Objection enumerating three invalid purposes for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three-part objection that bodily resurrection appears purposeless and why each proposed purpose is deemed invalid.

Core Idea
The objection claims resurrection is either futile or serves an unworthy purpose.

In this passage, the objector argues that bodily resurrection cannot have a meaningful purpose. They consider three possibilities—futility, a purpose for God, or a purpose for creatures—and find each unacceptable for a wise agent. This objection challenges the very rationale for resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall argument. Then read the translation to confirm understanding.
Notice the logical structure: the objector enumerates three possibilities and rejects each.
2
Identify the three categories of purpose
The objector considers: 1) futility, 2) a purpose returning to God, 3) a purpose returning to creatures. Distinguish each and see why each is rejected.
The rejection of a purpose for creatures is further subdivided into pain and pleasure.
3
Reflect on the philosophical basis
Think about why the objector assumes a wise agent must act for a purpose and why that purpose cannot be futile or self-serving. This sets up the need for a refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - أن الإعادة لا لغرض عبث لا يليق بالحكيم ، ولغرض عائد إلى الله تعالى نقص يجب تنزيهه عنه، ولغرض عائد إلى العباد ايضاً باطل، لأنه إما إيصال ألم ، وهو لا يليق بالحكيم، وإما إيصال ،لذة ولا لذة في الوجود، سيما في عالم الحس. فكل ما يتخيل لذة فإنما هو خلاص عن الألم، ولا ألم في العدم أو الموت، ليكون الخلاص عنه لذة مقصودة بالإعادة ، بل إنما يتصور ذلك بأن يوصل إليه ألماً ثم يخلصه عنه، فتكون الاعادة لإيصال ألم يعقبه خلاص (۳) وهو غير لائق بالحكمة (٤) . والجواب - منع الزوم الغرض، وقبح الخلو عنه في فعل الله تعالى. ثم منع انحصار الغرض في إيصال اللذة والألم () ، إذ يجوز أن يكون نفس إيصال الجزاء إلى من يستحقه ،غرضاً ، ثم منع كون اللذة دفعاً للألم، وخلاصاً عنه . كيف واللذة والألم من الوجدانيات التي لا يشك العاقل في تحققها، وقد سبق تحقيق
Third — That restoration has no purpose: futility is unbefitting of the Wise; a purpose returning to God is a deficiency from which He must be exalted; and a purpose returning to the servants is also invalid, because it is either the delivery of pain, which is unbefitting of the Wise, or the delivery of pleasure, and there is no pleasure in existence, especially in the sensory world. For everything imagined as pleasure is but deliverance from pain, and there is no pain in non-existence or death such that deliverance from it would be a pleasure intended by restoration. Rather, that can only be imagined by delivering pain to one and then delivering him from it, so restoration would be for delivering pain followed by deliverance — and that is not befitting of wisdom. The answer: Denial of the necessity of purpose and the ugliness of being devoid of it in God's action. Then denial that purpose is restricted to delivering pleasure and pain, for it is possible that the very delivery of recompense to its deserving one is a purpose. Then denial that pleasure is repulsion of pain and deliverance from it. How so, when pleasure and pain are among the direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt) whose reality no rational person doubts, and this has been established.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against bodily resurrection: it must have a purpose, but it cannot be futile, nor for God's benefit (since He transcends need), nor for the benefit of creatures (since that would involve either pain or pleasure, and pleasure is merely removal of pain, but there is no pain in death). Thus resurrection would cause unnecessary pain, which is unbefitting of a wise agent. The answer refutes each point: first, God is not subject to needing a purpose; second, the purpose is precisely to deliver just recompense; third, pleasure is not merely the removal of pain—pleasure and pain are direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt) whose reality is self-evident, as has been established elsewhere.

Key Terms
الغرض
العبث
الحكيم
اللذة
الألم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why is a purpose returning to creatures invalid?
A) Because it would involve delivering pain, which is unbefitting of the Wise.
B) Because it would involve delivering pleasure, and pleasure does not exist in the sensory world.
C) Both A and B are reasons.
D) Because creatures do not deserve any recompense.

Key Takeaway
The objection asserts that resurrection cannot have a purpose consistent with divine wisdom, as all possible purposes are shown to be invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector claims that all pleasure is merely relief from pain. Think of the last time you felt true pleasure—was it really just an escape from discomfort? How does this observation unsettle your understanding of why you seek pleasure in this life?
?
If you cannot think of a single purpose for your own resurrection that satisfies the criteria of wisdom (no futility, no deficiency in God, no cycle of pain), does that shake your confidence in the afterlife? What would you say to the objector face to face?
?
The objection argues that delivering pain as a purpose is unbefitting of the Wise. Yet you know that God has created a world with immense suffering. How do you reconcile this with the objection's claim? Is the objection valid, or is there a purpose beyond your grasp?

The Refutation: Three Denials
Refutation of the objection through three denials.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three-pronged refutation that denies the necessity of purpose, the restriction of purpose to pain/pleasure, and the reducibility of pleasure to pain removal.

Core Idea
The answer shows that God is not bound by purpose, recompense itself is a purpose, and pleasure is an irreducible experience.

In this passage, the author directly counters the objection by denying its key assumptions. He first denies that God must act for a purpose at all. Then he denies that purpose is limited to delivering pain or pleasure. Finally, he denies that pleasure is merely the removal of pain, insisting that pleasure and pain are direct, self-evident experiences.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the three instances of 'منع' (denial).
The answer is concise but powerful.
2
Identify the three denials
List the three denials: 1) Denial of the necessity of purpose in God's actions. 2) Denial that purpose is restricted to pleasure/pain. 3) Denial that pleasure is merely relief from pain.
Each denial targets a specific claim in the objection.
3
Understand the justification for each denial
For the first, the author simply asserts that purpose is not necessary. For the second, he states that delivering just recompense is a valid purpose. For the third, he appeals to the self-evident nature of pleasure and pain as direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt).
The third denial is supported by a reference to prior proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - أن الإعادة لا لغرض عبث لا يليق بالحكيم ، ولغرض عائد إلى الله تعالى نقص يجب تنزيهه عنه، ولغرض عائد إلى العباد ايضاً باطل، لأنه إما إيصال ألم ، وهو لا يليق بالحكيم، وإما إيصال ،لذة ولا لذة في الوجود، سيما في عالم الحس. فكل ما يتخيل لذة فإنما هو خلاص عن الألم، ولا ألم في العدم أو الموت، ليكون الخلاص عنه لذة مقصودة بالإعادة ، بل إنما يتصور ذلك بأن يوصل إليه ألماً ثم يخلصه عنه، فتكون الاعادة لإيصال ألم يعقبه خلاص (۳) وهو غير لائق بالحكمة (٤) . والجواب - منع الزوم الغرض، وقبح الخلو عنه في فعل الله تعالى. ثم منع انحصار الغرض في إيصال اللذة والألم () ، إذ يجوز أن يكون نفس إيصال الجزاء إلى من يستحقه ،غرضاً ، ثم منع كون اللذة دفعاً للألم، وخلاصاً عنه . كيف واللذة والألم من الوجدانيات التي لا يشك العاقل في تحققها، وقد سبق تحقيق
Third — That restoration has no purpose: futility is unbefitting of the Wise; a purpose returning to God is a deficiency from which He must be exalted; and a purpose returning to the servants is also invalid, because it is either the delivery of pain, which is unbefitting of the Wise, or the delivery of pleasure, and there is no pleasure in existence, especially in the sensory world. For everything imagined as pleasure is but deliverance from pain, and there is no pain in non-existence or death such that deliverance from it would be a pleasure intended by restoration. Rather, that can only be imagined by delivering pain to one and then delivering him from it, so restoration would be for delivering pain followed by deliverance — and that is not befitting of wisdom. Then denial that purpose is restricted to delivering pleasure and pain, for it is possible that the very delivery of recompense to its deserving one is a purpose. Then denial that pleasure is repulsion of pain and deliverance from it. How so, when pleasure and pain are among the direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt) whose reality no rational person doubts, and this has been established.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against bodily resurrection: it must have a purpose, but it cannot be futile, nor for God's benefit (since He transcends need), nor for the benefit of creatures (since that would involve either pain or pleasure, and pleasure is merely removal of pain, but there is no pain in death). Thus resurrection would cause unnecessary pain, which is unbefitting of a wise agent. The answer refutes each point: first, God is not subject to needing a purpose; second, the purpose is precisely to deliver just recompense; third, pleasure is not merely the removal of pain—pleasure and pain are direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt) whose reality is self-evident, as has been established elsewhere.

الغرض
اللذة
الألم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pleasure is merely the removal of pain.
Correction: Pleasure and pain are direct experiences (al-wijdāniyyāt) whose reality is self-evident, not reducible to each other.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three denials in the answer?
A) Denial that purpose is necessary in God's actions.
B) Denial that purpose is restricted to pleasure and pain.
C) Denial that delivering recompense can be a purpose.

Refuting the Purpose Objection to Resurrection
Al-Taftazani refutes the objection that resurrection without a purpose is absurd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Taftazani refutes the objection that bodily resurrection must serve a purpose, using the method of 'prevention' (manʿ) to block each premise.

Core Idea
Resurrection's purpose is not pleasure or pain, but just recompense.

In this passage, al-Taftazani addresses a sophisticated objection against bodily resurrection based on the necessity of purpose for a wise agent. The objector argues that any purpose for resurrection would be either for God (deficient) or for servants (impossible). The response uses a series of 'preventions' to dismantle the objection, showing that purpose can be simply giving what is due.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: the objection is presented first, followed by the answer with multiple 'preventions'.
The objection is summarized in the first part, and the answer begins with 'والجواب'.
2
Identify the objection's three parts
The objector argues that resurrection cannot have a purpose: not for God (implies deficiency), not for servants (reduces to pleasure or pain, which are impossible). Identify these parts.
The objection is framed as 'Third: That resurrection...'.
3
Analyze the four preventions
The answer consists of four 'manʿ' (prevention) statements. Note each one: denying necessity of purpose, denying restriction to pleasure/pain, denying that pleasure is mere release from pain, and denying that hereafter pleasures are same as worldly.
Each prevention blocks a premise of the objection.
4
Reflect on the method
Consider how this argument uses logical denial rather than positive proof. It shows that the objector's premises are not necessary, so the objection fails.
This is a common dialectical method in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - أن الإعادة لا لغرض عبث لا يليق بالحكيم، ولغرض عائد إلى الله تعالى نقص يجب تنزيهه عنه، ولغرض عائد إلى العباد أيضاً باطل، لأنه إما إيصال ألم، وهو لا يليق بالحكيم، وإما إيصال لذة ولا لذة في الوجود، سيما في عالم الحس. فكل ما يتخيل لذة فإنما هو خلاص عن الألم، ولا ألم في العدم أو الموت، ليكون الخلاص عنه لذة مقصودة بالإعادة، بل إنما يتصور ذلك بأن يوصل إليه ألماً ثم يخلصه عنه، فتكون الإعادة لإيصال ألم يعقبه خلاص وهو غير لائق بالحكمة. والجواب - منع اللزوم الغرض، وقبح الخلو عنه في فعل الله تعالى. ثم منع انحصار الغرض في إيصال اللذة والألم، إذ يجوز أن يكون نفس إيصال الجزاء إلى من يستحقه غرضاً، ثم منع كون اللذة دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه. كيف واللذة والألم من الوجدانيات التي لا يشك العاقل في تحققها، وقد سبق تحقيق ذلك، ثم منع كون اللذات الأخروية من جنس الدنيوية بحسب الحقيقة ليلزم كونها دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه.
Third: That resurrection is not without a purpose—absurdity is not befitting the Wise; and for a purpose returning to God is a deficiency from which He must be exalted; and for a purpose returning to the servants is also false, because it is either causing pain, which is not befitting the Wise, or causing pleasure, and there is no pleasure in existence, especially in the sensible world. For everything imagined as pleasure is only a release from pain, and there is no pain in non-existence or death, so that release from it could be a pleasure intended by resurrection. Rather, that is only conceived by causing pain to him and then releasing him from it, so resurrection would be for causing pain followed by release, which is not befitting wisdom. The answer: Prevention of the necessity of purpose and the ugliness of lacking it in God's act. Then prevention of the restriction of purpose to causing pleasure and pain, for it is permissible that the very giving of recompense to the one who deserves it is a purpose. Then prevention that pleasure is a repulsion of pain and a release from it. How? For pleasure and pain are among the intuitive experiences whose reality no rational person doubts, and its investigation has preceded. Then prevention that the pleasures of the Hereafter are of the same kind as worldly pleasures in reality, so that they would necessarily be a repulsion of pain and a release from it.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection against bodily resurrection (al-iʿāda) based on the concept of purpose (al-gharaḍ). The objector argues that resurrection must have a purpose, but it cannot have a purpose: it cannot be for God (as that implies deficiency), nor for the servants, because any purpose for them reduces to causing pleasure or pain. They claim there is no real pleasure in existence, and imagined pleasure is merely release from pain; since there is no pain in non-existence, resurrection cannot aim at release from pain. Thus resurrection would be for causing pain followed by release, which is unbefitting wisdom. The answer (al-jawāb) consists of several 'preventions' (manʿ): First, the necessity of purpose in God's acts is denied. Second, the restriction of purpose to pleasure and pain is denied; giving recompense to the deserving can be a purpose. Third, the claim that pleasure is merely repulsion of pain is denied, as pleasure and pain are distinct intuitive experiences. Fourth, even if that were true, the pleasures of the Hereafter are not of the same nature as worldly pleasures, so the objection collapses. The argument follows a standard kalam format: objection then multiple 'manʿ' responses, each blocking a premise.

Key Terms
الإعادة
الغرض
اللذة
الألم
الحكيم
منع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the objection is about God's need for purpose; actually it's about the absurdity of purposeless action for a wise agent.
Correction: The objection is that a wise being cannot act without a purpose, not that God needs something. The refutation shows purpose is not required or is of a different kind.

Checkpoint
What is the main basis of the objector's argument that resurrection cannot have a purpose?
A) Resurrection must either cause pleasure or pain, but neither is possible.
B) Resurrection is impossible because bodies decay.
C) God cannot perform actions that involve time.
D) The soul does not survive death.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani refutes the purpose-based objection by denying its premises and expanding the concept of divine purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector claims all pleasure is merely relief from pain. When you look at your own desire for Paradise, is it driven more by fear of Hell or by a positive longing for the beatific vision? What would change if you truly believed the pleasures of the Hereafter are of an entirely different kind, not just a compensation for worldly suffering?
?
Al-Taftazani argues that God does not need a purpose to act wisely. Do you sometimes find yourself questioning God's wisdom in your trials because you cannot see a purpose? How can this lesson's reminder that God's wisdom is not bound by human purposes reshape your response to unexplained hardships?
?
The objector assumes that resurrection must either give pleasure or pain, but al-Taftazani asserts that the very act of giving recompense is a purpose in itself. How does that shift your understanding of the Day of Judgment—from a transaction of rewards and punishments to a profound display of divine justice? In what way does that make you more conscious of your deeds even when no immediate consequence is visible?

Understanding Spiritual Resurrection: Definition and Possibilities
Al-Taftazani defines spiritual resurrection and states it needs no further proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of spiritual resurrection presented by al-Taftazani and why he considers it automatically proven once the soul's survival is established.

Core Idea
Spiritual resurrection is the soul's return to its original state or its reattachment to the body.

Al-Taftazani begins this note by asserting that proving the soul's abstraction and survival after death automatically proves spiritual resurrection. He then defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to pure abstraction, free from bodily attachments, or it becomes attached to the resurrected body. This lesson explores these definitions and the initial claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source passage once through, then the translation. Focus on the first part where the claim and definitions are given.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find where al-Taftazani says 'it is either... or...'. Note the two possibilities: return to pure abstraction or attachment to the resurrected body.
The second possibility is immediately criticized as not intelligible or transmitted.
3
Understand the claim of no further proof
Why does al-Taftazani say that after proving the soul's survival, spiritual resurrection needs no extra proof? Because it is simply the soul's return to its original state or reattachment.
The proof of the soul's survival already establishes that the soul can exist without the body.
4
Consider the problem with the second definition
Note the author's remark that attachment to the resurrected body is 'neither intelligible nor transmitted'. What does this imply about which definition is intended?
This suggests the primary meaning is the return to pure abstraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: تنبيه بعد إثبات تجرد النفس وبقائها بعد خراب البدن لا يفتقر إثبات المعاد الروحاني إلى زيادة بيان، لأنه عبارة إما عن عودها إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد المحض، أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق ملتذة أو متألمة بما اكتسبت، وإما عن تعلقها بالبدن المحشور الذي ليس بمعقول ولا منقول، إما أن تتعلق به نفس أخرى، وتبقى نفسها معطلة أو متعلقة ببدن آخر. القائلون بالمعاد الروحاني فقط، أو به وبالجسماني جميعاً هم الذين يقولون بأن النفوس الناطقة مجردة باقية لا تفنى بخراب البدن لما سيق من الدلائل، ويشهد بذلك نصوص من الكتاب والسنة، فلا حاجة للأولين إلى زيادة بيان في إثبات المعاد، لأنه عبارة عن عود النفس إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق وبقائها ملتذة بالكمال أو متألمة بالنقصان، ولا للآخرين بعد إثبات حشر الأجساد، لأن القول بإحياء البدن مع تعلق نفس أخرى به تدبر أمره وبقاء نفسه معطلة، أو متعلقة ببدن آخر غير مقبول عند العقل، ولا منقول من ونفسها مناسبة لذلك المزاج، آلفة به لم تفارقه إلا لانتفاء قابليته لتصرفاتها. فحين عادت القابلية، عاد التعلق لا محالة. وقد يقال إن قوله تعالى: {فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين} للذين أحسنوا الحسنى وزيادة ورضوان من الله أكبر إشارة إلى المعاد الروحاني، وكذا الأحاديث الواردة في حال أرواح المؤمنين.
He said: A note. After the proof of the soul's abstraction and its survival after the body's decay, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not require additional explanation, because it is either (the soul's) return to what it was of pure abstraction, or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain due to what it acquired; or (it consists of) its attachment to the resurrected body—which is neither intelligible nor transmitted—either that another soul attaches to it, and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both spiritual and bodily resurrection, are those who say that the rational souls are abstract, surviving, not perishing with the body's decay due to the evidences presented, and texts from the Book and the Sunnah testify to that. So the former have no need for additional explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of abstraction or dissociation from the darknesses of attachment, and its remaining experiencing pleasure by perfection or pain by deficiency. Nor do the latter (need additional explanation) after the proof of the gathering of bodies, because the assertion that the body is revived with another soul attached to it managing its affairs while its own soul remains idle or attached to another body is unacceptable to reason, nor is it transmitted—and its own soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not separating from it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when the capacity returns, attachment returns necessarily. It may be said that His statement, the Exalted, {No soul knows what has been hidden for them of comfort for the eyes} for those who do good, the best and more, and the pleasure of God is greater, is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths concerning the state of the souls of the believers.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbīh) by the author on spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī). It begins by stating that once the soul's abstraction and survival after bodily decay are proven, proving spiritual resurrection needs no further explanation. The author then defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to its original state of pure abstraction, or it dissociates from attachments while experiencing pleasure or pain from its acquisitions. Another possibility is attachment to the resurrected body, but that is not rationally or textually established. Those who accept only spiritual resurrection, or both spiritual and bodily, hold that rational souls are abstract and survive bodily decay, based on proofs from reason and revelation. The first group needs no further proof for spiritual resurrection. The second group, after proving bodily resurrection, need no further proof because the soul naturally reattaches to its familiar body when the body regains receptivity. The author quotes a Quranic verse (Sajdah 32:17) and mentions hadiths about the souls of believers as evidence for spiritual resurrection.

Key Terms
المعاد الروحاني
تجرد النفس
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spiritual resurrection means a completely new spiritual existence created independently.
Correction: Spiritual resurrection is the same soul returning to its original state of abstraction, not a new creation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Taftazani, what is the primary definition of spiritual resurrection?
A) The soul's attachment to a new resurrected body.
B) The soul's return to pure abstraction after dissociation from the body.
C) The soul's reincarnation in another body.
D) The soul's annihilation and recreation.

Key Takeaway
Spiritual resurrection is the soul's return to its original dissociation from bodily attachments, automatically proven once the soul's survival is established.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul were to be stripped of all bodily attachments right now, what would it experience—pleasure or pain? How do your daily choices today shape that answer?
?
You claim to believe that the soul survives death and returns to its original state. Does your lifestyle reflect that you are truly convinced, or do you live as if this world is all there is?
?
The passage says spiritual resurrection needs no further proof once the soul's abstraction is established. Does your certainty about the afterlife match that logical conclusion, or do you still harbor doubts that affect your actions? How will you address those doubts starting today?

Why Bodily Resurrection Implies Spiritual Resurrection
Al-Taftazani argues that bodily resurrection entails spiritual resurrection due to the soul's natural reattachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Taftazani's argument that those who affirm bodily resurrection do not need additional proof for spiritual resurrection because the soul naturally reattaches to its body.

Core Idea
The soul's natural attachment to its body ensures that bodily resurrection includes spiritual resurrection.

After presenting the definitions, al-Taftazani addresses two groups: those who affirm only spiritual resurrection and those who affirm both. He argues that for the latter, once bodily resurrection is proven, spiritual resurrection is automatically implied because the soul is suited to its body and reattaches when the body regains receptivity. This lesson examines that reasoning and its support from revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups
The author mentions 'those who affirm only spiritual resurrection' and 'those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection'. Both groups hold that the soul is abstract and survives.
They are distinguished by whether they accept bodily resurrection in addition.
2
Understand the argument for the second group
For those who affirm bodily resurrection, once bodily resurrection is proven, spiritual resurrection follows automatically. Why? Because the soul is naturally attached to its body and only left due to the body's loss of capacity. When the body is resurrected and regains capacity, the soul reattaches necessarily.
This argument relies on the soul's suitability (munāsaba) for its particular body.
3
Reject alternative possibilities
Al-Taftazani rejects the idea that another soul could attach to the body while the original soul remains idle or attaches elsewhere. This is unacceptable to reason and not supported by revelation.
The soul and body have a unique affinity; replacement is impossible.
4
Examine the scriptural evidence
The author quotes Quran 32:17 about the hidden comfort for the righteous and mentions hadiths about the state of believers' souls, indicating spiritual resurrection.
These texts are seen as indications (ishāra) of spiritual resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

Refuting the Equating of Pleasures and Defining Spiritual Resurrection
Refutation of equating pleasures and definition of spiritual resurrection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of equating worldly and otherworldly pleasures, and the two ways spiritual resurrection is defined after the soul's survival.

Core Idea
Spiritual resurrection is either the soul's return to incorporeality or its attachment to a resurrected body.

The author begins by rejecting the claim that otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones, which would reduce them to mere pain removal. He then introduces a crucial note: once the soul's incorporeality and survival are proven, spiritual resurrection requires no further proof. This lesson unpacks that note and the two definitions of spiritual resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of equating pleasures
Read the first sentence carefully. Notice how the author preemptively blocks a potential objection that would reduce otherworldly pleasures to mere relief from pain.
This refutation is a 'manع' (prevention) in kalam style.
2
Understand the note on spiritual resurrection
After the refutation, the author states that proving the soul's survival makes spiritual resurrection self-evident. Identify the two definitions he gives: (1) return to pure incorporeality, (2) attachment to a resurrected body.
He uses 'imma... aw' (either... or) structure.
3
Distinguish the two groups of believers
The author mentions those who affirm only spiritual resurrection and those who affirm both. Note that both groups agree on the soul's incorporeality and survival. The difference lies in whether they also accept bodily resurrection.
The first group needs no extra proof for spiritual resurrection; the second group already has proof for bodily gathering.
4
Analyze the argument about soul-body attachment
Read the passage where the author argues that a soul suited to a body does not leave it except due to loss of capacity. When capacity returns, attachment is inevitable. This supports the bodily resurrection view.
This argument relies on 'munasabah' (suitability) between soul and body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم منع كون اللذات الأخروية من جنس الدنيوية بحسب الحقيقة ليلزم كونها دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه . قال : تنبيه) (تنبيه) بعد إثبات تجرد النفس وبقائها بعد خراب البدن لا يفتقر إثبات المعاد الروحاني إلى زيادة بيان، لأنه عبارة إما عن عودها إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد المحض (۳) ، أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق ملتذة أو متألمة، بما اكتسبت (۳) وإما عن تعلقها بالبدن المحشور الذي ليس بمعقول ولا منقول، إما أن تتعلق به نفس أخرى، وتبقى نفسها معطلة أو متعلقة ببدن آخر . القائلون بالمعاد الروحاني فقط، أو به، وبالجسماني جميعاً هم الذين يقولون بأن النفوس الناطقة مجردة باقية لا تفنى بخراب البدن لما سيق من الدلائل، ويشهد بذلك نصوص من الكتاب والسنة، فلا حاجة للأولين إلى زيادة بيان في إثبات المعاد، لأنه عبارة عن عود النفس إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق وبقائها ملتذة بالكمال أو متألمة بالنقصان ولا للآخرين بعد إثبات حشر الأجساد، لأن القول بإحياء البدن مع تعلق نفس أخرى به تدبر أمره وبقاء نفسه معطلة، أو متعلقة ببدن آخر غير مقبول عند العقل، ولا منقول من ونفسها مناسبة لذلك المزاج، آلفة به لم تفارقه إلا لانتفاء قابليته لتصرفاتها. فحين عادت القابلية، عاد التعلق لا محالة. وقد يقال إن قوله تعالى : {فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين} (٤) للذين أحسنوا الحسنى وزيادة (٥) ورضوان من الله أكبر (٦) إشارة إلى المعاد الروحاني، وكذا الأحاديث الواردة في حال أرواح المؤمنين، وخصوصاً الصديقين والشهداء والصالحين، وأنها في حواصل طيور خضر في قناديل من نور معلقة تحت العرش، وإن كانت ظواهرها مشعرة بأن الأرواح من قبيل الأجسام على ما قال إمام الحرمين أن الأظهر عندنا أن الأرواح أجسام لطيفة مشابكة للأجسام المحسوسة، أجرى الله تعالى العادة باستمرار حياة الأجساد ما استمرت مشابكتها بها فإذا فارقها، يعقب الموت الحياة في استمرار العادة، ثم الروح يعرج به ، ويرفع في حواصل طيور خضر في الجنة، ويهبط به إلى سجين من الكفرة كما وردت فيه الآثار والحياة عرض يحيى به الجوهر . والروح يحيا بالحياة أيضاً إن قامت به الحياة، فهذا قولنا في الروح، كذا في الإرشاد.
Then he prevented that the otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones according to reality so that they would be repelling pain and deliverance from it. He said: A note. (Note) After establishing the soul's incorporeality and its survival after the body's destruction, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not need further elaboration, because it is either a return to what it was of pure incorporeality, or dissociation from the darkness of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain, according to what it acquired, or its attachment to the resurrected body which is neither rational nor transmitted, either that another soul attaches to it and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both it and bodily resurrection, are those who say that rational souls are incorporeal, surviving, not perishing with the body's destruction, due to the proofs that have been presented, and texts from the Book and Sunnah testify to that. So the first group needs no further explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of incorporeality or dissociation from the darkness of attachment and its remaining enjoying perfection or suffering deficiency. And the second group after proving the gathering of bodies, because the statement of reviving the body while another soul attaches to it to manage its affair and its own soul remains idle, or attached to another body, is not acceptable to reason, nor transmitted from... And its soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not leaving it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when capacity returns, attachment returns inevitably. And it may be said that His statement, exalted: 'No soul knows what joy is kept hidden for them' ... is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths reported about the state of the souls of believers, especially the truthful, martyrs, and righteous, that they are in the crops of green birds in lanterns of light hung under the Throne, even if their apparent meanings suggest that souls are of the type of bodies, according to what Imam al-Haramayn said: the apparent view with us is that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, God, exalted, has made the habit continue of the life of bodies as long as their intertwining with them continues. So when it leaves them, death follows life in the continuation of habit. Then the soul ascends, is raised in the crops of green birds in Paradise, and is brought down to Sijjin of the disbelievers as reported in the traditions. And life is an accident that gives life to the substance. And the soul also lives by life if life subsists in it. This is our saying about the soul, as in al-Irshad.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage begins with a refutation of the claim that otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones, which would imply they are merely the removal of pain. Then the author introduces a note (تنبيه) on spiritual resurrection. He states that after proving the soul's incorporeality and survival after the body's destruction, proving spiritual resurrection requires no further explanation. He defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to its original disembodied state, free from attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain based on its deeds; or it attaches to a resurrected body that is neither knowable by reason nor reported. The author then distinguishes between two groups: those who affirm only spiritual resurrection (and need no extra proof) and those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. For the latter, after proving bodily resurrection, the soul's attachment to its original body is necessary if the soul is suited to that body. He cites Quranic verse 32:17 as evidence for spiritual resurrection, and mentions hadiths about the souls of believers being in the crops of green birds in lanterns under the Throne. He notes that these texts in their apparent meaning suggest that souls are bodies, and reports Imam al-Haramayn's view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, such that life continues as long as the intertwining lasts. The passage concludes with a summary: life is an accident that gives life to the substance, and the soul lives by life. This is the view expressed in al-Irshad.

Key Terms
المعاد الروحاني
التجرد
المعاد الجسماني
النفس الناطقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Scriptural Evidence and the Nature of Souls
Scriptural evidence for spiritual resurrection and discussion of the nature of souls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic and hadith evidence for spiritual resurrection and the author's discussion of whether souls are subtle bodies.

Core Idea
Apparent scriptural evidence suggests souls are subtle bodies, but the essence of resurrection is spiritual.

The author cites Quranic verse 32:17 and several hadiths about the souls of believers in green birds' crops under the Throne. He addresses the implication that these texts seem to depict souls as bodies, and reports Imam al-Haramayn's view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with physical bodies. This lesson examines that evidence and the author's concluding remarks on life and the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its interpretation
The author quotes verse 32:17 as an indication of spiritual resurrection. Notice how he interprets 'no soul knows what joy is kept hidden' as referring to spiritual delights beyond physical description.
The verse is often cited in discussions of spiritual reward.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the description of believers' souls in green birds' crops in lanterns under the Throne. Understand that these texts, in their apparent meaning, suggest souls are bodies.
Imam al-Haramayn is quoted to clarify this apparent meaning.
3
Analyze Imam al-Haramayn's view on souls
He states that the apparent view is that souls are subtle bodies (ajsam latifa) intertwined with sensible bodies. Life continues as long as this intertwining lasts.
This view attempts to reconcile scriptural language with philosophical concepts.
4
Understand the author's conclusion
The passage concludes by stating that life is an accident that gives life to the substance, and the soul lives by life. This is the position of the Ash'ari school as found in al-Irshad.
The soul is not itself an accident but a substance that receives life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم منع كون اللذات الأخروية من جنس الدنيوية بحسب الحقيقة ليلزم كونها دفعاً للألم وخلاصاً عنه . قال : تنبيه) (تنبيه) بعد إثبات تجرد النفس وبقائها بعد خراب البدن لا يفتقر إثبات المعاد الروحاني إلى زيادة بيان، لأنه عبارة إما عن عودها إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد المحض (۳) ، أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق ملتذة أو متألمة، بما اكتسبت (۳) وإما عن تعلقها بالبدن المحشور الذي ليس بمعقول ولا منقول، إما أن تتعلق به نفس أخرى، وتبقى نفسها معطلة أو متعلقة ببدن آخر . القائلون بالمعاد الروحاني فقط، أو به، وبالجسماني جميعاً هم الذين يقولون بأن النفوس الناطقة مجردة باقية لا تفنى بخراب البدن لما سيق من الدلائل، ويشهد بذلك نصوص من الكتاب والسنة، فلا حاجة للأولين إلى زيادة بيان في إثبات المعاد، لأنه عبارة عن عود النفس إلى ما كانت عليه من التجرد أو التبرؤ من ظلمات التعلق وبقائها ملتذة بالكمال أو متألمة بالنقصان ولا للآخرين بعد إثبات حشر الأجساد، لأن القول بإحياء البدن مع تعلق نفس أخرى به تدبر أمره وبقاء نفسه معطلة، أو متعلقة ببدن آخر غير مقبول عند العقل، ولا منقول من ونفسها مناسبة لذلك المزاج، آلفة به لم تفارقه إلا لانتفاء قابليته لتصرفاتها. فحين عادت القابلية، عاد التعلق لا محالة. وقد يقال إن قوله تعالى : {فلا تعلم نفس ما أخفي لهم من قرة أعين} (٤) للذين أحسنوا الحسنى وزيادة (٥) ورضوان من الله أكبر (٦) إشارة إلى المعاد الروحاني، وكذا الأحاديث الواردة في حال أرواح المؤمنين، وخصوصاً الصديقين والشهداء والصالحين، وأنها في حواصل طيور خضر في قناديل من نور معلقة تحت العرش، وإن كانت ظواهرها مشعرة بأن الأرواح من قبيل الأجسام على ما قال إمام الحرمين أن الأظهر عندنا أن الأرواح أجسام لطيفة مشابكة للأجسام المحسوسة، أجرى الله تعالى العادة باستمرار حياة الأجساد ما استمرت مشابكتها بها فإذا فارقها، يعقب الموت الحياة في استمرار العادة، ثم الروح يعرج به ، ويرفع في حواصل طيور خضر في الجنة، ويهبط به إلى سجين من الكفرة كما وردت فيه الآثار والحياة عرض يحيى به الجوهر . والروح يحيا بالحياة أيضاً إن قامت به الحياة، فهذا قولنا في الروح، كذا في الإرشاد.
Then he prevented that the otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones according to reality so that they would be repelling pain and deliverance from it. He said: A note. (Note) After establishing the soul's incorporeality and its survival after the body's destruction, the proof of spiritual resurrection does not need further elaboration, because it is either a return to what it was of pure incorporeality, or dissociation from the darkness of attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain, according to what it acquired, or its attachment to the resurrected body which is neither rational nor transmitted, either that another soul attaches to it and its own soul remains idle or attached to another body. Those who affirm only spiritual resurrection, or both it and bodily resurrection, are those who say that rational souls are incorporeal, surviving, not perishing with the body's destruction, due to the proofs that have been presented, and texts from the Book and Sunnah testify to that. So the first group needs no further explanation in proving resurrection, because it is the soul's return to what it was of incorporeality or dissociation from the darkness of attachment and its remaining enjoying perfection or suffering deficiency. And the second group after proving the gathering of bodies, because the statement of reviving the body while another soul attaches to it to manage its affair and its own soul remains idle, or attached to another body, is not acceptable to reason, nor transmitted from... And its soul is suitable for that temperament, familiar with it, not leaving it except due to the loss of its capacity for its actions. So when capacity returns, attachment returns inevitably. And it may be said that His statement, exalted: 'No soul knows what joy is kept hidden for them' ... is an indication of spiritual resurrection, and likewise the hadiths reported about the state of the souls of believers, especially the truthful, martyrs, and righteous, that they are in the crops of green birds in lanterns of light hung under the Throne, even if their apparent meanings suggest that souls are of the type of bodies, according to what Imam al-Haramayn said: the apparent view with us is that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, God, exalted, has made the habit continue of the life of bodies as long as their intertwining with them continues. So when it leaves them, death follows life in the continuation of habit. Then the soul ascends, is raised in the crops of green birds in Paradise, and is brought down to Sijjin of the disbelievers as reported in the traditions. And life is an accident that gives life to the substance. And the soul also lives by life if life subsists in it. This is our saying about the soul, as in al-Irshad.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage begins with a refutation of the claim that otherworldly pleasures are of the same genus as worldly ones, which would imply they are merely the removal of pain. Then the author introduces a note (تنبيه) on spiritual resurrection. He states that after proving the soul's incorporeality and survival after the body's destruction, proving spiritual resurrection requires no further explanation. He defines spiritual resurrection in two ways: either the soul returns to its original disembodied state, free from attachment, experiencing pleasure or pain based on its deeds; or it attaches to a resurrected body that is neither knowable by reason nor reported. The author then distinguishes between two groups: those who affirm only spiritual resurrection (and need no extra proof) and those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. For the latter, after proving bodily resurrection, the soul's attachment to its original body is necessary if the soul is suited to that body. He cites Quranic verse 32:17 as evidence for spiritual resurrection, and mentions hadiths about the souls of believers being in the crops of green birds in lanterns under the Throne. He notes that these texts in their apparent meaning suggest that souls are bodies, and reports Imam al-Haramayn's view that souls are subtle bodies intertwined with sensible bodies, such that life continues as long as the intertwining lasts. The passage concludes with a summary: life is an accident that gives life to the substance, and the soul lives by life. This is the view expressed in al-Irshad.

Three Schools on the Annihilation of the Body
Listing three positions on body annihilation with proponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct opinions among Islamic theologians on how the annihilation of bodies occurs.

Core Idea
Annihilation of bodies is debated among three causes: direct removal, opposite, or missing condition.

After establishing that bodies can be annihilated, theologians differed on the mechanism. Some said God directly annihilates, others said He creates an opposite that destroys, and others said a necessary condition is removed. This passage outlines those positions and their key proponents.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the three main schools. Notice the labels: الأول, الثاني, الثالث.
The passage is a list; look for the structure.
2
Identify sub-opinions
Within each school, note the different theologians and their specific views. For example, Abu al-Hudhayl vs. al-Qadi in the first school.
3
Reflect on incompleteness
The third school is cut off mid-sentence. Consider how the list might continue based on the pattern of the first two schools.
The source text ends with 'وقال أكثر' (and most said...).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثالث اختلف القائلون بصحة فناء الجسم في أنه بإعدام معدم، أو بحدوث ضد، أو بانتفاء شرط. أما الأول - فقال القاضي وبعض المعتزلة هو بإعدام الله تعالى بلا واسطة. وقال أبو الهذيل (۱) : بأمر إفن، كالوجود بأمر كن . وأما الثاني - فقال ابن الأخشيد (۳) : يخلق الله تعالى الفناء في جهة معينة، فتفنى الجواهر بأسرها. وقال ابن شبيب (۳) : يخلق الله في كل جوهر فناء، فيقتضي فناءه الزمان الثاني. وقال أبو علي : يخلق بعدد كل جوهر فناء، لا في محل . وقال أبو هاشم (٤) : بل فناء واحداً . وأما الثالث ـ فقال بشر (ه): ذلك الشرط بقاء يخلقه الله، لا في محل . وقال أكثر
The third investigation: Those who affirm the correctness of the annihilation of the body differed whether it is by the non-existence of an annihilator, or by the occurrence of an opposite, or by the absence of a condition. As for the first: al-Qadi and some of the Mu'tazila said it is by God's non-existence without intermediary. And Abu al-Hudhayl said: by a command 'Be annihilated', like existence by a command 'Be'. As for the second: Ibn al-Akhshid said: God creates annihilation in a specific direction, so all atoms perish. And Ibn Shabib said: God creates annihilation in every atom, so its annihilation necessitates the second time. And Abu Ali said: He creates as many annihilations as atoms, not in a locus. And Abu Hashim said: rather one annihilation. As for the third: Bishr said: that condition is a survival that God creates, not in a locus. And most said...
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the different opinions among those who affirm the annihilation of the body (فناء الجسم) regarding its cause. The author divides the debate into three main schools. The first school holds that annihilation occurs by direct removal (إعدام) by God, either without an intermediary (al-Qadi and some Mu'tazila) or by a direct command 'Be annihilated' (Abu al-Hudhayl, comparing to creation by 'Be'). The second school holds that annihilation occurs by the creation of an opposite (ضد). Sub-opinions include: Ibn al-Akhshid says God creates annihilation in a specific direction causing all atoms to perish; Ibn Shabib says God creates annihilation in each atom, causing its perishing in the second moment; Abu Ali says He creates as many annihilations as atoms, not in a locus; Abu Hashim says only one annihilation suffices. The third school holds that annihilation occurs by the removal of a condition (انتفاء شرط). Bishr states that the condition is a survival (بقاء) created by God not in a locus. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'وقال أكثر' (and most said...), indicating the enumeration continues beyond the window.

Key Terms
فناء الجسم
إعدام
حدوث ضد
انتفاء شرط
بقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all theologians agreed on a single cause for annihilation.
Correction: The passage shows at least three distinct schools with multiple sub-opinions, indicating significant disagreement.

Checkpoint
According to the text, which school holds that annihilation occurs by the absence of a condition?
A) The first school
B) The second school
C) The third school
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The cause of body annihilation is a disputed topic among theologians, with three main explanatory frameworks: direct annihilation, creation of an opposite, or removal of a condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a complex theological debate like this, do you tend to simplify it by favoring one side, or do you patiently examine each position as the scholars did? Reflect on a recent situation where you dismissed a view too quickly. What will you do differently next time?

These theologians devoted their lives to precise thinking about God's actions. Is there an area in your life where you are content with vague or inherited beliefs? What is one specific assumption you hold about God that you have never examined with this level of care, and what step will you take to investigate it?
